resources\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003cSPAN\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003c/H3\u003e\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cSPAN\u003e\u003cSTRONG\u003eOn-premises SSO systems:\u0026nbsp;\u003c/STRONG\u003e\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003cSPAN\u003eDeprecate any\u0026nbsp;on-premises\u0026nbsp;federation and Web Access Management infrastructure and configure applications to use Azure AD.\u0026nbsp;\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003cSPAN\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cSPAN\u003e\u003cSTRONG\u003eSaaS and LOB applications that support modern authentication protocols:\u0026nbsp;\u0026nbsp;\u003c/STRONG\u003e\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory/manage-apps/what-is-single-sign-on\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003eUse Azure AD for single sign-on\u003c/A\u003e\u003cSPAN\u003e.\u0026nbsp;The more apps you\u0026nbsp;configure to use\u0026nbsp;Azure AD\u0026nbsp;for authentication,\u0026nbsp;the less risk in\u0026nbsp;the case\u0026nbsp;of an on-premises\u0026nbsp;compromise\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003cSPAN\u003e.\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cSPAN\u003e\u003cSTRONG\u003eLegacy Applications\u0026nbsp;\u003c/STRONG\u003e\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003cSPAN\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/SPAN\u003e\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eAuthentication,\u0026nbsp;authorization, and remote access to legacy applications that do not support modern authentication can be enabled via\u0026nbsp;\u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory/manage-apps/application-proxy\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003eAzure AD Application Proxy\u003c/A\u003e. \u0026nbsp;They can also be enabled through a network or application delivery controller solution using\u0026nbsp;\u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory/manage-apps/secure-hybrid-access\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003e secure hybrid access partner integrations\u003c/A\u003e.\u0026nbsp;\u0026nbsp;\u0026nbsp;\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cSPAN\u003eChoose a VPN vendor that supports modern authentication and integrate its authentication with Azure AD.\u0026nbsp;In the case of an on-premises compromise, you can use Azure AD to disable or block access by disabling the VPN. \u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cSTRONG\u003eApplication and workload servers \u0026nbsp;\u003c/STRONG\u003e\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eApplications or resources that required servers can be migrated to Azure IaaS and use \u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory-domain-services/overview\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003eAzure AD Domain Services\u003c/A\u003e (Azure AD DS) to decouple trust and dependency on AD on-premises. To achieve this decoupling, virtual networks used for Azure AD DS should not have connection to corporate networks.\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eFollow the guidance of the \u003cA href=\"https://aka.ms/TierModel\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003ecredential tiering\u003c/A\u003e\u003cSPAN\u003e.\u003c/SPAN\u003e \u003cSPAN\u003eApplication Servers are typically considered Tier 1 assets.\u003c/SPAN\u003e\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003cH3 id=\"community-1751754-toc-hId--2124209538\"\u003e\u003cBR /\u003eConditional Access Policies\u003c/H3\u003e\n\u003cP\u003eUse Azure AD Conditional Access to interpret signals and make authentication decisions based on them. For more information, see the \u003cA href=\"https://aka.ms/deploymentplans/ca\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003eConditional Access deployment plan.\u003c/A\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory/fundamentals/auth-sync-overview\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003eLegacy Authentication Protocols\u003c/A\u003e:\u003cSTRONG\u003e \u0026nbsp;\u003c/STRONG\u003eUse Conditional Access to \u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory/conditional-access/howto-conditional-access-policy-block-legacy\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003eblock legacy authentication\u003c/A\u003e protocols whenever possible. Additionally, disable legacy authentication protocols at the application level using application-specific configuration.\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eSee specific details for\u0026nbsp; \u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/exchange/clients-and-mobile-in-exchange-online/disable-basic-authentication-in-exchange-online#how-basic-authentication-works-in-exchange-online\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003eExchange Online\u003c/A\u003e and\u0026nbsp; \u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/powershell/module/sharepoint-online/set-spotenant?view=sharepoint-ps\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003eSharePoint Online\u003c/A\u003e.\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eImplement the recommended \u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/microsoft-365/security/office-365-security/identity-access-policies?view=o365-worldwide\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003eIdentity and device access configurations. \u003c/A\u003e\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eIf you are using a version of Azure AD that does not include Conditional Access, ensure that you are using the \u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory/fundamentals/concept-fundamentals-security-defaults\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003eAzure AD security defaults\u003c/A\u003e.\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eFor more information on Azure AD feature licensing, see the \u003cA href=\"https://azure.microsoft.com/pricing/details/active-directory/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003eAzure AD pricing guide\u003c/A\u003e.\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u003cSTRONG\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/STRONG\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cH3 id=\"community-1751754-toc-hId--331860184\"\u003eMonitoring \u0026nbsp;\u0026nbsp;\u003c/H3\u003e\n\u003cP\u003eOnce you have configured your environment to protect your Microsoft 365 from an on-premises compromise, \u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory/reports-monitoring/overview-monitoring\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003eproactively monitor\u003c/A\u003e the environment.\u003cBR /\u003e\u003cBR /\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u003cSTRONG\u003eScenarios to Monitor\u003c/STRONG\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003eMonitor the following key scenarios, in addition to any scenarios specific to your organization. For example, you should proactively monitor access to your business-critical applications and resources.\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cSTRONG\u003eSuspicious\u0026nbsp;activity\u003c/STRONG\u003e: All\u0026nbsp;\u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/active-directory/identity-protection/overview-identity-protection#risk-detection-and-remediation\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003eAzure AD risk events\u003c/A\u003e\u0026nbsp;should be monitored for suspicious activity. \u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/active-directory/identity-protection/overview-identity-protection\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003eAzure AD Identity Protection\u003c/A\u003e\u0026nbsp;is natively integrated with Azure Security Center.\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eDefine the network\u0026nbsp;\u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/active-directory/reports-monitoring/quickstart-configure-named-locations\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003enamed locations\u003c/A\u003e\u0026nbsp;to avoid noisy detections on location-based signals.\u0026nbsp;\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cSTRONG\u003eUser Entity Behavioral Analytics (UEBA)\u0026nbsp;alerts\u003c/STRONG\u003e\u003cU\u003e:\u003c/U\u003e\u0026nbsp;Use UEBA to get insights on anomaly detection.\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eMicrosoft Cloud App Discovery (MCAS) provides\u0026nbsp;\u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/cloud-app-security/tutorial-ueba\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003eUEBA in the cloud\u003c/A\u003e.\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eYou can integrate\u0026nbsp;\u003cU\u003eon-prem UEBA from Azure ATP\u003c/U\u003e. MCAS reads signals from Azure AD Identity Protection.\u0026nbsp;\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cSTRONG\u003eEmergency access accounts activity\u003c/STRONG\u003e\u003cU\u003e:\u0026nbsp;\u003c/U\u003eAny access using\u0026nbsp;\u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory/roles/security-emergency-access\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003eemergency access accounts\u003c/A\u003e\u003cSPAN\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/SPAN\u003eshould be monitored and\u0026nbsp;\u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory/users-groups-roles/directory-emergency-access#monitor-sign-in-and-audit-logs\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003ealerts\u003c/A\u003e\u0026nbsp;created for investigations. This monitoring must include:\u0026nbsp;\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eSign-ins.\u0026nbsp;\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eCredential management.\u0026nbsp;\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eAny updates on group memberships.\u0026nbsp;\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eApplication Assignments.\u0026nbsp;\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cSTRONG\u003ePrivileged role activity\u003c/STRONG\u003e\u003cU\u003e:\u003c/U\u003e\u0026nbsp;Configure and review security\u0026nbsp;\u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/active-directory/privileged-identity-management/pim-how-to-configure-security-alerts?tabs=new#security-alerts\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003ealerts generated by Azure AD PIM\u003c/A\u003e. Monitor direct assignment of privileged roles outside PIM by generating alerts whenever a user is assigned directly.\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cSTRONG\u003eAzure AD tenant-wide\u0026nbsp;configurations\u003c/STRONG\u003e\u003cU\u003e:\u003c/U\u003e\u0026nbsp;Any change to tenant-wide configurations should generate alerts in the system.\u0026nbsp;These include but are not limited to\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eUpdating custom through direct federation or social logins)\u0026nbsp;\u0026nbsp;\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eConditional Access or Risk policy changes\u0026nbsp;\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cSTRONG\u003eApplication of the custom role definitions\u0026nbsp;\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eNew custom roles created\u0026nbsp;\u003cBR /\u003e\u003cBR /\u003e\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u003cSTRONG\u003eLog Management\u003c/STRONG\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003eDefine a log storage and playbooks.\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cSTRONG\u003eAzure AD Logs \u003c/STRONG\u003eIngest logs and signal produced following consistent best practices (e.g., diagnostics settings, log retention, SIEM ingestion, etc.).\u0026nbsp;The log strategy must include the following Azure AD logs: \u0026nbsp;\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eSign-in activity\u0026nbsp;\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eAudit logs\u0026nbsp;\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eRisk events\u0026nbsp;\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003cP class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\" style=\"padding-left : 30px;\"\u003eAzure AD provides\u0026nbsp;\u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory/reports-monitoring/concept-activity-logs-azure-monitor\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003eAzure Monitor integration\u003c/A\u003e\u0026nbsp;for the sign-in activity log and audit logs. Risk events can be ingested through\u0026nbsp;\u003cA href=\"https://aka.ms/AzureADSecuredAzure/32b\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003eMicrosoft Graph API\u003c/A\u003e.\u0026nbsp;You can \u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory/reports-monitoring/howto-integrate-activity-logs-with-log-analytics\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003estream Azure AD logs to Azure monitor logs\u003c/A\u003e.\u003cBR /\u003e\u003cBR /\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cSTRONG\u003eHybrid Infrastructure OS Security Logs.\u003c/STRONG\u003e\u0026nbsp;All hybrid identity infrastructure OS logs should be archived and carefully monitored as a Tier 0 system, given the surface area implications. This includes:\u0026nbsp;\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eAzure AD Connect. \u003cA href=\"https://aka.ms/AzureADSecuredAzure/32e\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"\u003eAzure AD Connect Health\u003c/A\u003e\u0026nbsp;must be deployed to monitor identity synchronization.\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eApplication Proxy Agents\u0026nbsp;\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003ePassword\u0026nbsp;write-back agents\u0026nbsp;\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003ePassword Protection Gateway machines\u0026nbsp;\u0026nbsp;\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eNPS that have the Azure MFA RADIUS extension\u0026nbsp;\u003cBR /\u003e\u003cBR /\u003e\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003cH2 id=\"community-1751754-toc-hId-2026569930\"\u003eStay up to date\u003c/H2\u003e\n\u003cP\u003eThe Solarwinds attack is an ongoing investigation, and our teams continue to act as first responders to these attacks. As new information becomes available, we will make updates through our Microsoft Security Response Center (MSRC) blog at \u003cA href=\"https://nam06.safelinks.protection.outlook.com/?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcomm.microsoft.com%2FPoliteMail245%2Fdefault.aspx%3Fpage%3DmOgDA41300uL7Q32_8nsGA%26ref_id%3DKI8WohcEM0KIdOtHZj3pQw\u0026amp;data=04%7C01%7Cadhall%40microsoft.com%7Ca48f35f285d94ccd698f08d8a3956502%7C72f988bf86f141af91ab2d7cd011db47%7C1%7C0%7C637439209352849256%7CUnknown%7CTWFpbGZsb3d8eyJWIjoiMC4wLjAwMDAiLCJQIjoiV2luMzIiLCJBTiI6Ik1haWwiLCJXVCI6Mn0%3D%7C1000\u0026amp;sdata=Xebz37S3gWRu3E8WvV1FRMz6vDhcBRDY0uQCZi9ogEc%3D\u0026amp;reserved=0\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\"\u003ehttps://aka.ms/solorigate\u003c/A\u003e.\u003c/P\u003e","body@stringLength":"29225","rawBody":"\u003cP\u003eMany customers connect their private corporate networks to Microsoft 365 to benefit their users, devices, and applications. However, there are many well-documented ways these private networks can be compromised. As we have seen in \u003cA href=\"https://blogs.microsoft.com/on-the-issues/2020/12/13/customers-protect-nation-state-cyberattacks/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"\u003erecent events related to the SolarWinds compromise\u003c/A\u003e, on-premises compromise can propagate to the cloud. Because Microsoft 365 acts as the “nervous system” for many organizations, it is critical to protect it from compromised on-premises infrastructure.\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003eThis document will show you how to configure your systems to protect your Microsoft 365 cloud environment from on-premises compromise. We primarily focus on Azure AD tenant configuration settings, the ways Azure AD tenants can be safely connected to on-premises systems, and the tradeoffs required to operate your systems in ways that protect your cloud systems from on-premises compromise.\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003eWe strongly recommend you implement this guidance to secure your Microsoft 365 cloud environment.\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cH2\u003eUnderstanding primary threat vectors from compromised on-premises environments\u003c/H2\u003e\n\u003cP\u003eYour Microsoft 365 cloud environment benefits from an extensive monitoring and security infrastructure. Using machine learning and human intelligence that looks across worldwide traffic can rapidly detect attacks and allow you to reconfigure in near-real-time. In hybrid deployments that connect on-premises infrastructure to Microsoft 365, many organizations delegate trust to on-premises components for critical authentication and directory object state management decisions. Unfortunately, if the on-premises environment is compromised, these trust relationships result in attackers’ opportunities to compromise your Microsoft 365 environment.\u003cBR /\u003e\u003cBR /\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003eThe two primary threat vectors are \u003cSTRONG\u003efederation trust relationships\u003c/STRONG\u003e and \u003cSTRONG\u003eaccount synchronization. \u003c/STRONG\u003eBoth vectors can grant an attacker administrative access to your cloud.\u003cBR /\u003e\u003cBR /\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cOL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cSTRONG\u003eFederated trust relationships\u003c/STRONG\u003e, such as SAML authentication, are used to authenticate to Microsoft 365 via your on-premises Identity Infrastructure. If a SAML token signing certificate is compromised, federation would allow anyone with that certificate to impersonate any user in your cloud\u003cSTRONG\u003e. We recommend you disable federation trust relationships for authentication to Microsoft 365 when possible.\u003cBR /\u003e\u003cBR /\u003e\u003c/STRONG\u003e\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cSTRONG\u003eAccount synchronization\u003c/STRONG\u003e can be used to modify privileged users (including their credentials) or groups granted administrative privileges in Microsoft 365. \u003cSTRONG\u003eWe recommend you ensure that synchronized objects hold no privileges beyond a user\u003c/STRONG\u003e \u003cSTRONG\u003ein Microsoft 365, \u003c/STRONG\u003eeither directly or via inclusion in trusted roles or groups. Ensure these objects have no direct or nested assignment in trusted cloud roles or groups.\u003cBR /\u003e\u003cBR /\u003e\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/OL\u003e\n\u003cH2\u003ePrinciples for Protecting Microsoft 365 from on-premises compromise\u003c/H2\u003e\n\u003cP\u003eTo address the threat vectors outlined above, we recommend you adhere to the principles illustrated below: \u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u003cLI-IMAGE width=\"999\" height=\"568\" alt=\"SLO1.PNG\" align=\"inline\" id=\"241815iAFF55B566995BFF1\" size=\"large\" sourcetype=\"new\"\u003e\u003c/LI-IMAGE\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cDIV id=\"tinyMceEditordarlenebada_0\" class=\"mceNonEditable lia-copypaste-placeholder\"\u003e\u0026nbsp;\u003c/DIV\u003e\n\u003cOL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cSTRONG\u003eFully Isolate your Microsoft 365 administrator accounts.\u003c/STRONG\u003e They should be\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eMastered in Azure AD.\u0026nbsp;\u0026nbsp;\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eAuthenticated with Multi-factor authentication (MFA).\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eSecured by Azure AD conditional access.\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eAccessed only by using Azure Managed Workstations.\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/OL\u003e\n\u003cP class=\"lia-indent-padding-left-30px\"\u003eThese are restricted use accounts. \u003cSTRONG\u003eThere should be no on-premises accounts with administrative privileges in Microsoft 365. \u003c/STRONG\u003eFor more information see this \u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/microsoft-365/admin/add-users/about-admin-roles?view=o365-worldwide\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"\u003eoverview of Microsoft 365 administrator roles\u003c/A\u003e. Also see \u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory/roles/m365-workload-docs\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"\u003eRoles for Microsoft 365 in Azure Active Directory\u003c/A\u003e.\u003cBR /\u003e\u003cBR /\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cOL start=\"2\"\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cSTRONG\u003eManage devices from Microsoft 365. \u003c/STRONG\u003eUse Azure AD Join and cloud-based mobile device management (MDM) to eliminate dependencies on your on-premises device management infrastructure, which can compromise device and security controls.\u003cBR /\u003e\u003cBR /\u003e\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cSTRONG\u003eNo on-premises account has elevated privileges to Microsoft 365.\u003c/STRONG\u003e Accounts accessing on-premises applications that require NTLM, LDAP, or Kerberos authentication need an account in the organization’s on-premises identity infrastructure. Ensure that these accounts, including service accounts, are not included in privileged cloud roles or groups and that changes to these accounts cannot impact the integrity of your cloud environment. Privileged on-premises software must not be capable of impacting Microsoft 365 privileged accounts or roles.\u003cBR /\u003e\u003cBR /\u003e\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cSTRONG\u003eUse Azure AD cloud authentication \u003c/STRONG\u003eto eliminate dependencies on your on-premises credentials\u003cSTRONG\u003e. \u003c/STRONG\u003eAlways use strong authentication, such as Windows Hello, FIDO, the Microsoft Authenticator, or Azure AD MFA.\u003cBR /\u003e\u003cBR /\u003e\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/OL\u003e\n\u003cH2\u003eSpecific Recommendations\u003c/H2\u003e\n\u003cP\u003eThe following sections provide specific guidance on how to implement the principles described above.\u003cBR /\u003e\u003cBR /\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cH3\u003eIsolate privileged identities\u003c/H3\u003e\n\u003cP\u003eIn Azure AD, users with privileged roles such as administrators are the root of trust to build and manage the rest of the environment. Implement the following practices to minimize the impact of a compromise.\u003cBR /\u003e\u003cBR /\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eUse cloud-only accounts for Azure AD and Microsoft 365 privileged roles.\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eDeploy \u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory/devices/howto-azure-managed-workstation\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"\u003eAzure Managed Workstations\u003c/A\u003e for privileged access to manage Microsoft 365 and Azure AD.\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eDeploy \u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory/privileged-identity-management/pim-configure\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"\u003eAzure AD Privileged Identity Management\u003c/A\u003e\u003cSPAN\u003e (PIM)\u003c/SPAN\u003e for just in time (JIT) access to all human accounts that have privileged roles, and require strong authentication to activate roles.\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eProvide administrative roles the \u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory/roles/delegate-by-task\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"\u003eleast privilege possible to perform their tasks\u003c/A\u003e.\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eTo enable a richer role assignment experience that includes delegation and multiple roles at the same time, consider using Azure AD security groups or Microsoft 365 Groups (collectively “cloud groups”) and \u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory/roles/groups-assign-role\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"\u003eenable role-based access control\u003c/A\u003e\u003cSPAN\u003e. \u003c/SPAN\u003e\u0026nbsp;You can also use \u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory/roles/administrative-units\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"\u003eAdministrative Units\u003c/A\u003e to restrict the scope of roles to a portion of the organization.\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eDeploy \u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory/roles/security-emergency-access\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"\u003eEmergency Access Accounts\u003c/A\u003e and do NOT use on-premises password vaults to store credentials. \u0026nbsp;\u003cBR /\u003e\u003cBR /\u003e\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003cP\u003eFor more information, see \u003cA href=\"https://aka.ms/SPA\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"\u003eSecuring privileged access\u003c/A\u003e, which has detailed guidance on this topic. \u0026nbsp;Also, see \u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory/roles/security-planning\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"\u003eSecure access practices for administrators in Azure AD\u003c/A\u003e.\u003cBR /\u003e\u003cBR /\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cH3\u003eUse cloud authentication\u003c/H3\u003e\n\u003cP\u003eCredentials are a primary attack vector. Implement the following practices to make credentials more secure.\u003cBR /\u003e\u003cBR /\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory/authentication/howto-authentication-passwordless-deployment\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"\u003eDeploy passwordless authentication\u003c/A\u003e: Reduce the use of passwords as much as possible by deploying passwordless credentials. These credentials are managed and validated natively in the cloud. Choose from:\u003cBR /\u003e\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/windows/security/identity-protection/hello-for-business/passwordless-strategy\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"\u003eWindows Hello for business\u003c/A\u003e\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory/authentication/howto-authentication-passwordless-phone\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"\u003eAuthenticator App\u003c/A\u003e\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory/authentication/howto-authentication-passwordless-security-key-windows\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"\u003eFIDO2 security keys\u003c/A\u003e\u003cBR /\u003e\u003cBR /\u003e\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003e\u003cA href=\"https://aka.ms/deploymentplans/mfa\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"\u003eDeploy Multi-Factor Authentication\u003c/A\u003e: Provision \u003cA href=\"https://docs.microsoft.com/azure/active-directory/fundamentals/resilience-in-credentials\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"\u003emultiple strong credentials using Azure AD MFA\u003c/A\u003e. That way, access to cloud resources will require a credential that is managed in Azure AD in addition to an on-premises password that can be manipulated.\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eFor more information, see \u003cA href=\"https://aka.ms/resilientaad\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"\u003eCreate a resilient access control management strategy with Azure active Directory\u003c/A\u003e.\u003cBR /\u003e\u003cBR /\u003e\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003c/UL\u003e\n\u003cP\u003e\u003cSTRONG\u003eLimitations and tradeoffs\u003cBR /\u003e\u003c/STRONG\u003e\u003c/P\u003e\n\u003cUL\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eHybrid account password management requires hybrid components such as password protection agents and password writeback agents. \u0026nbsp;If your on-premises infrastructure is compromised, attackers can control the machines on which these agents reside. While this will not compromise your cloud infrastructure, your cloud accounts will not protect these components from on-premises compromise.\u003c/LI\u003e\n\u003cLI\u003eOn-premises accounts synced from Active Directory are marked to never expire in Azure AD, based on the assumption that on-premises AD password policies will mitigate this.
